# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# Kafka Log Retention Policy Configuration Audit

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that enforce log retention policy: the log.retention.ms and log.retention.bytes validation, the LogManager retention check, and the segment deletion enforcement for both time-based and size-based retention.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I have successfully identified all Java source files in apache/kafka that enforce log retention policy and created a comprehensive analysis at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

I found **7 key Java/Scala source files** that implement log retention policy enforcement:

1. **UnifiedLog.java** - Core segment deletion implementation with time-based and size-based retention methods
2. **LogManager.scala** - Orchestrates periodic retention checks through `cleanupLogs()`
3. **LogConfig.java** - Validates retention configuration values
4. **RemoteLogManager.java** - Extends retention enforcement to remote/tiered log segments
5. **DynamicBrokerConfig.scala** - Validates dynamic configuration updates for retention policies
6. **ServerLogConfigs.java** - Defines retention configuration constants
7. **RemoteLogManagerConfig.java** - Defines remote storage retention configuration

## Key Enforcement Components

The retention policy enforcement follows this execution chain:
- **LogManager.cleanupLogs()** → periodically triggered
- **UnifiedLog.deleteOldSegments()** → checks retention conditions
- **deleteRetentionMsBreachedSegments()** → enforces time-based retention (log.retention.ms)
- **deleteRetentionSizeBreachedSegments()** → enforces size-based retention (log.retention.bytes)
- **RemoteLogManager retention handlers** → for tiered storage scenarios

The answer file includes all relevant files, symbols (methods), execution chains, and a detailed narrative explaining the complete retention policy enforcement mechanism in Kafka.

When remote log storage is enabled with copy enabled, they use the local retention values; otherwise, they use the global retention values.\\n\\n## Configuration and Validation\\n\\n**LogConfig (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogConfig.java)** provides validation methods for retention configuration:\\n\\n- **validateBrokerLogConfigValues() (lines 494-500)**: Entry point for broker-level validation that calls remote storage-specific validators when remote log storage is enabled.\\n- **validateRemoteStorageRetentionSize() (lines 578-592)**: Validates that when log.retention.bytes is set, the log.local.retention.bytes value is not -1 and does not exceed log.retention.bytes.\\n- **validateRemoteStorageRetentionTime() (lines 595-609)**: Validates that when log.retention.ms is set, the log.local.retention.ms value is not -1 and does not exceed log.retention.ms.\\n\\n## Dynamic Configuration Updates\\n\\n**DynamicBrokerConfig (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/DynamicBrokerConfig.scala)** handles dynamic configuration changes:\\n\\n- **validateLogLocalRetentionMs() (lines 664-676)**: Validates changes to log local retention time, ensuring it doesn't exceed log.retention.ms when both are configured.\\n- **validateLogLocalRetentionBytes() (lines 679-691)**: Validates changes to log local retention bytes, ensuring it doesn't exceed log.retention.bytes when both are configured.\\n\\n## Remote Log Manager Integration\\n\\n**RemoteLogManager (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/log/remote/storage/RemoteLogManager.java)** extends retention enforcement to remote log segments:\\n\\n- **RemoteLogRetentionHandler inner class (lines 1116-1200)**: Contains the retention checking logic for remote segments.\\n- **isSegmentBreachedByRetentionSize() (lines 1131-1152)**: Checks if a remote segment exceeds the size-based retention threshold.\\n- **isSegmentBreachedByRetentionTime() (lines 1154-1171)**: Checks if a remote segment exceeds the time-based retention threshold based on the segment's maximum timestamp.\\n\\n## Configuration Constants\\n\\n**ServerLogConfigs (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/config/ServerLogConfigs.java)** and **RemoteLogManagerConfig (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/log/remote/storage/RemoteLogManagerConfig.java)** define the configuration properties:\\n\\n- LOG_RETENTION_TIME_MILLIS_CONFIG: Time-based retention threshold in milliseconds\\n- LOG_RETENTION_BYTES_CONFIG: Size-based retention threshold in bytes\\n- LOG_CLEANUP_INTERVAL_MS_CONFIG: Frequency of retention checks (default 300 seconds)\\n- LOG_LOCAL_RETENTION_MS_CONFIG: Local retention time for tiered storage\\n- LOG_LOCAL_RETENTION_BYTES_CONFIG: Local retention bytes for tiered storage\\n\\nThe entire retention enforcement system is designed to work at both the broker level (affecting all topics) and the topic/partition level (allowing per-topic customization), with special handling for tiered/remote log storage scenarios.\"\n}\n",
